You was extremely frightened. Upon careful examination, he traced the handwriting to Li Kunquan, a worker in the mill. He immediately took the letter to the sixth public security branch and reported it. The police arrested Li for questioning. Li's confession was evasive. He was immediately ordered to write a confession, and the handwriting was found to be the same. He was then sent to the County Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Yangzhou 69

Jiangdu Local Elementary Schools Still Unable to Resume Classes: The educational funding in Jiangdu is extremely scarce, so there are often strikes and demands for salaries. Currently, due to arrears in educational expenses, excluding the old debts, there are a total of nine months' worth, resulting in repeated suspensions of classes, which has not been resolved for six weeks. On the administrative side, the goal is to raise and distribute one month's expenses by the end of the year (estimated at 16,000 yuan). However, the teachers and staff aim to distribute three months' worth of funds at once, which is too far apart, resulting in a stalemate. It seems difficult to realize the resumption of classes this semester.

Difficult to Construct Riverbank Breaches Due to Freezing of the Canal: Since the 27 breaches in the canal, the people have been running around and appealing, hoping that the government will start construction as soon as possible to remedy the situation. However, although the government has stipulated four million yuan for the post-disaster construction funds, only one million yuan has been received to date, which is too far short of the target. Yesterday (the 11th), a strong northeast wind blew, and the entire canal froze very thickly. If the weather does not warm up, it will be difficult to start construction on the breaches for a while, and the people along the canal and those related to the canal bank are all worried.

Hangzhou 72

Bandit Leader Wu Tianbao Executed by Firing Squad Yesterday: The Zhejiang Provincial Government stated that Wu Tianbao, the bandit leader from Fenghua, also known as Wu A'gen and Wu Binghui, had colluded with bandits Jiang A'xing, Lin Si'hu, and more than 30 others in the 17th year of the Republic of China, each carrying firearms, to carry out arson and robbery in Fenghua, turning the entire town into scorched earth and killing the company commander and several soldiers of the Provincial Merit Army. Afterwards, he repeatedly committed hundreds of cases of robbery and kidnapping. The bandit party was particularly numerous. After a strict arrest, he was hiding in the French Concession in Shanghai. The Security Department sent Detective Zhong Yun to arrest him, but he was shot and killed, and several detectives from the detective office were injured. After being arrested, personnel were sent to escort the bandit leader Ying Yang to Hangzhou. The Provincial Government ordered a trial, and he confessed without hesitation. He was sentenced to death. At 9:00 AM on the 12th, the bandit was taken out to verify his identity and escorted to the execution ground outside Qingbo Gate to be executed by firing squad.

At the same time, there are also two old public bonds for reorganization and repayment that should be repaid with interest, totaling tens of thousands of silver dollars in interest payments. The Finance Department believes that the current financial situation has reached a desperate situation and it is difficult to cope. Therefore, it has sent separate letters to the three public bond funds, approving a half-month extension for repayment.

Education News Special Feature

Outline of National Salvation Activities for Elementary Schools, by Chen Pin-yi 74

Since the outbreak of the national crisis, many national salvation activity plans for elementary schools have been published by the education sector. However, upon closer examination, these documents mostly list activities directly. The authors inevitably omit or overlook details, or they are too superficial. The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education initiated the Shanghai Municipal Elementary and Secondary School National Humiliation Eradication and National Salvation Center Activities. Due to my duties, I gathered the opinions of colleagues within the school and considered educational principles and the current situation with the goal of carefully implementing this work. Based on the pragmatist principles of "this time" and "this place," I drafted a general implementation plan. The implementation process has proven to be useful. I am now publishing it to study together with colleagues in elementary education on the implementation plan for the National Humiliation Eradication and National Salvation Center Activities.

Purpose: Implement nationalist education, inspire and cultivate children's patriotic thoughts and emotions.

Implementation Principles: Taking the resistance against Japan and national salvation as the goal, teaching and guidance as the tools, and children as the objects, reasonable stimulation will be applied to obtain appropriate responses.

Activity Outline

Implementation Period: Starting from September 23 (the date of the national mourning assembly ordered by the central government), with a period of one month. Extension is possible if necessary.

Points to Note During Implementation

(1) Guiding Children's Thoughts: (1) Promote the essence of nationalism to strengthen children's determination to unite and save the nation; (2) Promote the essence of "benevolence" and "humanity" to cultivate children's concept of defending "justice"; (3) Introduce the attitudes of various countries around the world towards the events in the Northeast to cultivate children's international perspective.

(2) Guiding Children's Emotions: (1) Arouse children's sense of vigilance, but avoid fear; (2) Inspire children's high-spirited emotions, but avoid impulsiveness; (3) Train children's calm attitude, but avoid pessimism.

News

Ministry of Education's Statement on Early Holiday Admonition at National Central University 75

Dismissal of Two Directors Untrue

Regarding the matter of the students of National Central University petitioning the Ministry of Education, a reporter specifically went to the Ministry to meet with Directors Jiang and Sun. According to them, "The three points raised by the students of National Central University during their petition to the Ministry were: (1) Revoke the order for early holidays; (2) Approve Zhu Jia-hua's resignation; (3) During the transition period, the Ministry should order professors to manage the school. At the time, the Vice Ministers were not at the Ministry, so the two of us went out to meet the students successively. Regarding the first point, because the Ministry did not indeed have an order for early holidays, we told them the truth. Regarding the second and third points, we agreed to convey these intentions to the Minister and have the Ministry forward them to the National Government for approval. The students proposed a written reply, so the two of us signed and sealed the reply, which the students found satisfactory and returned to school together. Later, we reported the process to the Vice Ministers, who informed us that Minister Li had already sent a handwritten note to President Zhu on the evening of the 8th regarding the matter of ordering early holidays for Central University, and stated that a formal order would be issued the next day. Because the Minister was attending a meeting at the Central Party Headquarters, he did not inform the Higher Education Department about the handwritten note he had sent, so the Higher Education Department was completely unaware. The formal order was indeed only completed and delivered to Central University at 5 PM on the 9th.

Furthermore, the Political News Agency published news the day before yesterday, stating that Director Sun Ben-wen of the Higher Education Department of the Ministry of Education had resigned to take responsibility and had been approved, but the successor had not yet been announced. It was also rumored that Director Jiang Shao-mo of the General Affairs Department also intended to resign. According to a statement from the responsible personnel of the Ministry of Education, both of these news items are untrue. Directors Sun and Jiang are still performing their duties as before and have not resigned to the Ministry."

Representative Meeting of the Anti-Japanese Association of Middle School Students 78

Re-election of Executive Committee and Presidium

Meeting Continues at 10 AM This Morning

The United Association of Anti-Japanese National Salvation of Secondary Schools held its ninth emergency representative meeting at Qinxin Middle School yesterday (the 12th) at 9 AM. Representatives from 43 middle schools attended, with Hui Zao and Li Bin, and Zhengfeng Fangmo serving as chairpersons, and Huang Shiti of Shanghai Middle School recording the details as follows:

Passed Resolutions: (1) Regarding whether or not to express an opinion on Wang Jingwei's prior advocacy of opening a National Salvation Congress (Resolution): After the association's representatives investigate Mr. Wang Jingwei, a decision will be made, with the executive committee assigning a standing executive member to be responsible. (2) Regarding whether or not member schools of this association should participate in today's (i.e., yesterday's) citizen assembly (Resolution): Not to participate. (4) Regarding whether or not to discuss the demonstration group going to Beijing (Resolution): No need to discuss. Those who wish to participate may sign up with the presidium and then organize it. (6) The presidium can also serve as the executive committee (Resolution): Passed. (7) Whether or not to set a date for resumption of classes (Resolution): No need to set a date for resumption of classes. (8) Re-election of the executive committee and the presidium (Resolution): Passed.

Elected Executive Committee: After resolving to re-elect, the executive committee and the presidium were elected. As a result, the following 19 schools were elected to the executive committee: Jingye (29 votes), Fudan Affiliated Middle School (26 votes), Provincial Shanghai Middle School (33 votes), Huiling (20 votes), Hujiang (29 votes), Patriotic (21 votes), Guanghua (21 votes), Dongwu No. 2 Middle School (7 votes), Datong Affiliated Middle School (17 votes), Wuben (20 votes), Chizhi (20 votes), Fudan Shizhong (18 votes), Pudong (20 votes), Minli (21 votes), Fisheries (17 votes), Qinxin (24 votes), Qixiu (19 votes), Minli Girls' Middle School (6 votes), Shanghai Girls' Middle School (16 votes). The schools elected to the presidium are: Hujiang (14 votes), Shanghai Middle School (13 votes), and Huiling (13 votes). After the election, as it was 6 PM, it was announced that the meeting would be adjourned and continue at Qinxin again at 10 AM this morning.

The Second Week of the Senior Cup: Donghua vs. Lehua 85

| Lehua's Amazing Performance |

| Result: One Goal Each |

Yesterday, Donghua Football Team, which drew a 0-0 tie with Jinan in Shenjiang, competed in the second week of the Senior Cup against Lehua at the Zhonghua Baseball Field, resulting in a 1-1 draw. Over eight hundred spectators attended. The two teams are currently tied, and will re-resolve the outcome as soon as possible to determine the right to re-compete for the cup. The details are described below:

Chatting about the Past and Present

The Donghua team has a wealth of talent, strong combat strength, and a well-deserved reputation. The Lincoln team was defeated by a score of 2 to 4. Previously, in the Western Union A Group competition, Donghua also defeated Yihua by a score of 5 to 1. Yihua has been steadily declining and is not worth mentioning. In the Western Union A Group, they have been defeated in every match and have never scored; even a draw has never happened. Given Donghua's prestige, Lehua was certainly not their opponent, so Shanghai football fans did not expect to see this. Unexpectedly, the fierce battle resulted in Donghua drawing with them at 1 to 1.

Donghua's Lineup

Yesterday's Donghua's lineup remained unchanged, with no major changes. Only Chen Yutian was absent, replaced by Chen Jiaqiu. Jiaqiu's right-wing performance was even better than Yutian's, but Jin Yuanqian's right midfielder was slightly weak. Tu Kaiyuan and Chen Pu also did not show a good performance. The internal guards controlled the overall situation for half the game. Wang Changying replaced Guan Xun'an, and Wang's performance was mediocre, occasionally leaving gaps. The forwards were as strong as ever, but they were unable to achieve any special success because Lehua's defenses were tight and there was no opportunity to be taken.

Lehua's Talent

The Lehua team has no well-known names, so it is not valued by people. It is an emerging force formed by the elites of Fudan and Jiaotong Universities, and there are high hopes for its future. Yesterday's performance was quite remarkable. Goalkeeper Lu Zhonghuan performed admirably, saving many dangerous balls. Among the entire team, only Sun Huipei and Chen Tao showed some weakness, while all other players were remarkable. Forwards Wan Xianghua and Zhou Shaowen were able to penetrate the enemy camp from time to time, but they missed good chances due to poor shooting, which was regrettable.

Gu Shangrang Sun Huipei

Lu Zhiming Wan Xianghua

Lu Zhongen Wang Shumiao Jiang Chao

Zhao Aichen Zhou Shaowen

Chen Chao Li Lin

Overview of the Situation

The overall situation was quite balanced, with equal opportunities for both sides and mutual dangers. Five minutes after the start, Donghua scored a goal by Dai Linjing. Afterwards, Lehua often took the offensive, but opportunities were frequently lost. By the fortieth minute, Lehua took advantage of a free kick and Wan Xianghua headed the ball into the net, making the score 1-1 in the first half. The second half passed peacefully, with nothing gained. As a result, a draw was made.

One Goal Each in the First Half

Lehua kicked off, and Donghua's soldiers advanced to spy. Chen Jiaqiu's passes were effective, and Dai Linjing shot at the goal, but it was released by Lu Zhongen. Before long, Dai dribbled the ball and attacked, shooting from about 16 yards from the goal. Lu Zhongen was about to catch the ball, but a gust of wind blew the ball towards the corner of the goal and into the net. Lu turned to save, but it was too late. After losing this goal, Lehua's spirit suddenly rose. Zhou Shaowen and Wan Xianghua had a total of four shots, but they were either saved or went out of bounds, and they did not gain any advantage. Later, Chen Pu touched the ball with his hand in front of the goal at 30 yards, committing a foul. Lehua's Wang Shusen took the free kick and lobbed it over Donghua's defense. Zhou Shaowen and Wan Xianghua seized the opportunity and chased after it. Zhou Xianyan was about to save the ball, but Wan Xianghua gained priority and headed the ball into the goal, making it 1-1 and ending the first half.

The Second Half Was Uneventful

At the start of the second half, Lehua went all out and pressed Donghua. The spirit was extremely invigorated. In front of Donghua's goal, there was a sense of tension. Lehua took another free kick 30 yards from Donghua's goal. Wang Shumiao's lob was effective and aimed directly at the goal. Zhou Xianyan took a lesson from the past and was careful to guard against danger. Donghua did not relax at this point, determined to win. Dai Linjing and Qian Jingyong both had shots, but they did not hit the target. Back and forth, they saw each other's safety. Forty-five minutes passed peacefully, with no achievements. In the end, it ended in a draw. The referee was Jiang Xiangqing.

The Children's Chicken (Part 1) 88

A Letter to Xu Junqi Zhou

I recently enjoyed studying natural science very much, so when I received the second issue of the Normal School Student Monthly, I turned to your "The Children's Chicken" and read both articles from beginning to end in one breath. I felt that they were extremely good. That a topic that seemed so small at first could provoke children to roll out questions like pearls, one after another, is such a beautiful art! I greatly admire your attitude of "knowing what you know, and admitting what you don't know" in responding to these questions. As I read the article, I felt as if I had become a child in your class, participating in the discussion. I put myself in that position and wondered, if I were a child in your class, what else would I like to ask? I thought about it carefully and prepared to make two requests: (1) Ask everyone to start hatching chickens at school or at home when the time is right; (2) Ask to explore the principles of chickens using scientific methods.

The evolution of educational methods can be roughly divided into four stages:

The first stage: Relying on the teacher to teach, not allowing students to ask questions;

The second stage: Teachers and students discuss together; questioning and challenging each other;

The third stage: Teachers and students learn by doing, teach by doing, discuss by doing, question and challenge each other by doing;

The fourth stage: Teachers and students use scientific methods to pursue the reason for doing, and discover ways to do better than now.

You have raised chickens at home yourself, so you can be considered to have reached the third stage. Your educational method, as expressed in this lesson, can only be considered to have reached the second stage. I think you are a very promising teacher. It is best not to linger in this second stage. You must immediately muster the courage to advance to the third and fourth stages.

The Chongming Man Who Vanquished the Japanese Pirates 89

— Zēng Lí

During the Jiajing era of the Ming dynasty, Japanese pirates invaded my Chongming. The magistrate, Tang Yicen, defended the county seat to the death. Outnumbered, he was ultimately defeated and died. At the time, a scholar named Gu Guoxuan heard that the city was under attack by the pirates. He immediately led many local militiamen, intending to assist the magistrate. Upon arrival, he found that the magistrate was dead and the city had already fallen. Gu then declared loudly to the crowd, "Magistrate Tang died for the people. We should also repay him with our lives!" At that time, the pirates had only broken into the city. Gu, drawing his sword, engaged them in battle. Before long, the pirates were greatly terrified and fled, leaving behind over two hundred dead. The city was then recovered by us. The governor reported the matter to the provincial government. The province ordered the military commissioner, Xiong Fu, to come to Chongming for inspection. Discovering that the battalion commander, Gao, was colluding with the pirates, he had him executed immediately. He petitioned for an honorary commendation for Magistrate Tang, who had died defending the city, and awarded cloth and silk to Gu's militia. The following year, the Japanese pirates invaded Taicang. Xiong then appealed to Gu, saying, "Chongming was spared from disaster entirely thanks to your efforts. Now Taicang is in critical danger. I implore you to assist me." Gu then led a thousand militiamen straight to Taicang and defeated the pirates in a single battle. When the pirates invaded Jiading and Suzhou, Gu again led the militia to pursue them. From then on, the Japanese pirates, upon encountering the Chongming militia, would invariably flee in fear. Alas, Gu Guoxuan, the scholar of my Chongming! At that time, there were many scholars in Chongming. Most of them cared only about their literary pursuits, grumbling about the work required to pass the imperial examinations. At the first sound of battle, they would cower in fear, not daring to step beyond their doorsteps. Gu Guoxuan alone understood the greater righteousness, disregarded death, and led the militia to defeat the Japanese pirates and recover the city. Moreover, neighboring towns relied on his strength to eliminate the pirates. His actions greatly increased the glory of my Chongming people. Now, Japan is invading and occupying our Eastern Provinces, yet the generals and officials of the Eastern Provinces do not dare to retaliate with a single arrow. Considering the actions of Gu Guoxuan, how can they not be ashamed to die?

World News in Brief 90

— Hǎi Kè

The Speed of Clothing Manufacture From the moment the wool is sheared from the sheep until the garment is finished, the fastest record has been held by the Americans, at six hours and four minutes. No one could match their speed. The British, not to be outdone, quickly caught up, achieving a time of three hours, twenty minutes, and thirty seconds, nearly twice as fast as the Americans. However, they were still not satisfied and sped up their process even further. Within days, they shaved off another hour, maintaining a record of two hours, nine minutes, and forty-six seconds to this day. This record seemed likely to stand for some time, with no one to surpass it. Who knew that it would soon meet a formidable opponent and be easily defeated by Australia? They sheared the wool from the sheep, wove the fabric, and made the clothes, completing all the work in just one hour, fifty-one minutes, and eighteen and a half seconds. This is truly like riding a special express train, leaving others in the dust. To catch up, one would need an airplane.

Recording Japan's Forcible Demolition of Roads 91

— Lǚ Bīng

The South Manchuria Railway, operated by Japan, is regarded as the sole source of profit for the empire's invasion of our Northeast Three Provinces. Therefore, they are willing to use violence to implement their road-building plans. However, from another perspective, they harbor extreme jealousy towards the extension of our nation's state-owned routes and constantly engage in sabotage. What I am about to describe occurred around 1929, when the Japanese used military force to demolish the Beining branch line, revealing their frightening ambition, enough to shock those who hear of it. However, at the time, local authorities exercised restraint and negotiated to prevent escalation. The Railway Gazette published an account of the incident in the previous year. I am therefore bringing it up now so that those concerned about Japanese atrocities may have it recorded.

Shenyang has long been known as a scenic spot, and the imperial tombs outside the city are particularly rich in historical sites. The eastern tomb, Fuling, is about ten miles from the city and is accessible by rail, making it convenient for tourists. On pleasant days in spring and autumn, crowds flock there. The scene is no less lively than the special train for watching the Qiantang River tidal bore. The northern tomb, Zhaoling, is close to the Zhen Gong Chang of Northeastern University. Although the scenery is beautiful, the travel back and forth is inconvenient, which travelers regret. The year before last, the Beining Railway Bureau obtained approval from the Northeast Transportation Committee to build a Zhaoling branch line to connect with it. During construction, the route had to pass through the Sakai Farm. This farm originally belonged to the Zhaoling subsidiary, but a Japanese named Sakai, in collusion with the tomb guards, privately leased it. The Japanese obstructed the project, causing complications. Subsequently, through reasoned arguments from the Diplomatic Affairs Office, a sum of 130,000 silver dollars was spent to redeem it. With this settled, it was thought that the matter was over. Unexpectedly, the Japanese were still dissatisfied and sought to sabotage the project. Suddenly, on a certain day, they dispatched a large team of plainclothes guards and armed military police from the South Manchuria Railway. They forcefully detained the stationmaster, deployed sentries, and demolished the already constructed road. Afterwards, they left triumphantly. Our government authorities could do nothing about it. At this time, the Northeast had not yet fallen, and the barbarity of the Japanese was already like this. It is clear that the more our country retreats, the more the enemy presses forward. To retreat without resistance is sure to lead to national subjugation.

A Daughter's Life 92

— Qǐ Wén Nǚshì

The status of women in our country's society has always been very low. Looking back at history, most women have always been treated as playthings or even slaves by men. Even though Bai Juyi's "Song of Everlasting Regret" contains the line "Do not value the birth of sons, value the birth of daughters," from his perspective, this precisely represents the shame women have suffered throughout Chinese history. How despicable is the ancient proverb, "A woman adorns herself for the pleasure of her man."

In modern times, the women's movement has become very popular. However, we cannot deny that this superficial glory still does not match the actual gains. Most rural women still groan under the iron heel of the old ethics, living lives of slavery. And the few women above the petty bourgeoisie are still holding onto the idea of selling their appearance, acting as playthings for men. Those who are more enlightened are only a very small minority of all women, and their strength is very weak, so success is naturally difficult to achieve.

The elevation of women's status still depends on our own active efforts. However, in the political aspect, the government of a country, for the sake of safeguarding the entire civil rights, must recognize that women and men should have equal treatment. Even in our country, the National Government has made many explicit provisions regarding the rights of women in recent years. Even the misconception that was considered a principle in the old society that women should not inherit property has been completely broken. This is naturally a very powerful inspiration, and it is also our most victorious gain.

However, the cruel traces left over from the old society have not yet been completely eliminated. In almost every old family, there are almost always strange dramas that run counter to the advocacy of women's rights. I recently saw a new film from the Star Film Company, called "Unfortunately Born a Daughter," which is a compilation of many strange dramas of old families, and depicts the story of women's repressed grievances.

It seems that there are many questions that every woman must ask herself: "Why is our society accustomed to valuing men over women?" "Why do men take concubines?" "Why do men seduce women?" We often do not have a clear answer to these many questions. However, in "Unfortunately Born a Daughter," there are many bizarre and wonderful explanations, which make us laugh so hard when we first see them, but then we want to cry out loud.

"Unfortunately Born a Daughter" may be to let our women let out a sigh of relief. We hope that it can awaken many illusions of the old society and give an effective help to the women's movement. I think every woman should go and see it, so that after receiving the enjoyment of some of the plot, they can understand part of the meaning of the women's movement.

Chatting at the Reading Window 93

— Gān Yí

Cen Chi (Part 1)

In past dynasties, there were hermits, but none quite like the one I will speak of in modern times. Dwelling in mountain springs, with eccentric habits different from the masses, I have found such a person. His name is Cen Chi, style name Shengzhi, from Shaoxing, Zhejiang. He is a registered student, well-versed in various books, and writes prose that is elegant and readable. He can compose ten thousand words in a short time, as if divinely assisted. His calligraphy is also outstanding. Moreover, he is skilled in cooking and sewing. He is capable in every way. His family was poor, so he made a living with his pen in various places. He once traveled thousands of miles to visit a relative in Jiangxi, who was working on something in Xincheng. Xincheng is our hometown, east of Ganzhou, surrounded by overlapping mountains, with narrow roads difficult for travelers. By the time Chi arrived, the person had already gone to the provincial capital, leaving Chi disappointed. Traveling was expensive, and he had no food or lodging. In a dilemma, he offered his skills in making clothes to the local tailors, hoping to gradually accumulate funds and then return to his hometown. The tailors, seeing his handsome appearance, did not believe him. However, they then saw him holding a needle and scissors, working as if he had practiced it for a long time. Surprised, they asked Chi about his background. Chi sighed and said, "Things have turned out unexpectedly. I had no choice. That I have fallen to this state can be said to be a calamity sent by Heaven." The tailor said, "Upon first meeting you, I recognized you as an extraordinary person. It turns out my eyes did not deceive me. You are a man of accomplishment. Take it easy and don't worry. The day when the dragon breaks through the wall will come." At that time, my late uncle Bao Shan (Jingmo), the Provincial Surveillance Commissioner of Gansu, had requested to retire due to illness and was about to spend the rest of his life in his hometown. During the New Year, he was visiting people when he saw a spring couplet on the door of a certain house. The wording was elegant and relevant, and the calligraphy was lively, seeming to dance. He judged that it could only have been written by a person of high talent and was very surprised. My late uncle and Lu Zhiyou (Qiguang) were known for their calligraphy. They often visited relatives and friends in the village, and he could recognize the handwriting of all the people. This was someone he had never seen before. Many local celebrities praised the work. In the end, they could not find out who it was. So he asked the owner of the house. The owner said, "This was written by a famous scholar. Even his casual conversation is extraordinary, and his handwriting is even more refined. It is fitting that you see it and praise it. He is currently stranded here and initially made a living as a tailor. Judging by his words and actions, he is not only a scholar but also a man of talent and a rare person. I have already treated him with the respect due to a teacher. He is about to return to Yue. You must meet him." My late uncle said, "Tonight, I will have the cook prepare a feast and wait for you to invite the old gentleman to come and chat." At dusk, the person came with Chi, delighted. Tall and slender, with an elegant bearing, they were seated. The host and guest regretted that they had not met sooner and discussed the classics of history and literature, as well as the way of painting and calligraphy. Everything Chi said was relevant. Finally, he described his family history in great detail. He was asked if he was married. He said no. My late uncle said, "This is a heaven-sent opportunity. My youngest daughter is not yet betrothed. She is talented, virtuous, and beautiful. Would she be suitable for you?"

Rotary Club Storytelling

Sharing the Enemy of Our Children (11) 94

— Gù Míngdào

Chapter Two: Like-Minded

That very evening, the soldiers of the Sun Country indeed launched their atrocities. The continuous gunshots startled all the students in the school. But in the darkness, they did not dare to act rashly. None of the telephones could get through. They had no choice but to close the school gates and wait quietly for what might happen. The next morning, the news spread. Many patriotic students were enraged. Hua Naiqiang suggested that if the Sun Country soldiers invaded the school, everyone should arm themselves and defend it, not allowing them to cross the line. However, because of other considerations, they were afraid of being implicated. While the discussion was still unresolved, the Sun Country soldiers arrived uninvited. The students had no choice but to flee for their lives. At this time, Zhongshu was in the upper floor and did not have time to escape. She had no choice but to hide in the room. Unexpectedly, the Sun Country soldiers had already spotted her. They broke down the door and entered. They saw Zhongshu's beautiful face and had evil thoughts. They wanted to commit violence. At this critical moment, one of them fell. It was not Zhongshu who was shot. It was when the soldier was raising his gun to fire that a bullet suddenly flew in from the window where Zhongshu was standing. It hit the soldier's head squarely. He fell to the ground with a thud. Then a short-clothed young man jumped in and shouted, "How dare you scoundrels be so rude!" The Sun Country soldier saw his companion shot and was shocked. He quickly raised his bayonet to stab the young man. The young man raised his hand and fired another shot, killing the soldier on the floor as well. At this time, Zhongshu recognized the young man as Hua Naiqiang. She was both surprised and delighted. Hua Naiqiang picked up the Mauser pistol from the soldier's hand and handed it to Zhongshu, saying, "The situation is urgent. Let's leave quickly." Zhongshu took the Mauser pistol without asking any questions. She followed him and jumped out of the room, running quietly downstairs. Hearing the sound of Sun Country soldiers shouting in front, they hurried to run to the back, around the back of the library. There was a small alleyway. At the end of the alleyway was a pile of short walls with some weeds growing on them. It was quiet and deserted. Hua Naiqiang turned his head and said, "Outside the wall is the wilderness. We can escape from here." Zhongshu stood still, hesitating. Hua Naiqiang understood what she meant. He walked to the wall and squatted down, saying, "You can stand on my shoulders. I will lift you up." Zhongshu did not care about anything else. She stepped on his shoulders. Hua Naiqiang stood up. Zhongshu grabbed the top of the wall with both hands. Carrying the Mauser pistol, she raised her body. Hua Naiqiang took the opportunity to lift her feet. Zhongshu had already climbed over the wall. Seeing that outside the wall was a grass field, she jumped down. Hua Naiqiang also hurriedly climbed onto the short wall. Just as he was about to go down, he suddenly saw a Sun Country soldier coming in with a gun. With a bang, a bullet flew towards Hua Naiqiang. (End of Chapter Two)

Gold Prices Fell Last Week in the Financial Market 95

Fluctuations Reached 60 Taels

Decline of 31.2 Taels

Reaction After Three Weeks of Rise In the past week, spot gold prices resumed their downward trend, a reaction from the three consecutive weeks of gains. However, the ever-changing situation was confusing, with no clear direction. The market was turbulent, with daily fluctuations of more than 20 taels, which was truly bewildering to investors. The market was weak from the beginning of the week, then fluctuated around 700 taels, as various unfavorable news from home and abroad spread. Only on Thursday did it rise to 708 taels. Subsequently, due to the sudden resignation of the Japanese cabinet and rumors of renewed gold export bans and abandonment of the gold standard, the market plummeted, with a catastrophic fall of 30 taels to a low of 649 taels. The total fluctuation for the week was 60 taels. By the end of the week, the market recovered slightly, with a net decline of 31.2 taels. Overseas silver markets and Shanghai's British and American exchange rates had increased. Bank trading prices of British gold exceeded 2 shillings, and US gold reached 34 yuan. Chinese merchants varied in their positions, with many remaining short. The brokers generally adopted a wait-and-see attitude. However, with the volatile situation, there was concern that the future would remain bleak. Initial margins ranged from 70 to 80 taels, then 50 to 60 taels, and even 100 taels at most, eventually settling around 70 taels. The delivery of physical gold was smooth, with raw gold increasing by about 6 taels. Yesterday (November 11), the silver report shrank, and today's gold prices may open higher. The general situation of the past week is summarized below.

Complex Psychology and Volatile Market Conditions On Monday (December 7), the silver report increased again by 1875, the silver price increased by 2.5 shillings, the spread widened by two levels, and the internal market was also loose. Most market participants were hedging, causing the gold price to fall by 7.8 taels at the opening, to 693 taels. It then rose to 96 taels due to strong buying. Reasons for Tight Silver Supply 98

Yesterday, a key figure in the financial world stated that the reason for the tightening silver supply was that Japanese commercial firms were selling goods, but were afraid to come forward themselves, so they entrusted foreign banks to collect the money on their behalf, no less than 300,000 to 400,000 per day. Local News

Rioters Infiltrated Yesterday's Citizen Assembly Causing Disturbances 108

More Than Ten Trams and Cars Were Destroyed

Chief Liu Escaped After Being Kidnapped

The Shanghai People's Anti-Japanese National Salvation United Association held a citizen assembly at the Nanshi Public Sports Ground at 6 pm yesterday. Because rioters infiltrated the assembly, they took the opportunity to riot and cause trouble during the parade and demonstration. The Municipal Public Security Bureau took strict precautions, preventing a major disaster. Many cars and trams were destroyed. The details of each item are recorded as follows:

Citizen Assembly Photography (Captured by This Newspaper) 109

A Glimpse of the Assembly There were more than 50 groups, including the National Advancement Association, Modern Middle School, Mingde Middle School, Northeastern Shanghai Fellow Association, Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Student Association in Japan, Anti-Japanese Association of Japanese Cotton Mill Workers, Striking Workers of Datong Bookstore, Anti-Japanese Association of Shanghai Eastern Cotton Weaving Industry, Shanghai Theater Troupe United Association, and Korean Anti-Japanese Association, with more than 500 representatives. Before the meeting, many red and white reactionary leaflets had been found in the venue. The assembly's discipline team, with yellow and white cloths wrapped around their arms, guarded the venue, only allowing people to enter and not to exit.

Chairman's Report Chairman Chen Gongyu, representative of the Northeastern Shanghai Fellow Association Anti-Japanese Association, reported, roughly saying that when Japanese imperialism is swallowing China, our compatriots are all slaves of a fallen nation. To save our compatriots, to restore our territory, our compatriots must unite and overthrow Japanese imperialism. After the presidium report, Kim Han, representative of the Korean Laborer and Rickshaw Workers Union, Liu Chuanchun, Miao Weihan, representative of the Shanghai Youth Anti-Japanese National Salvation Group, Sun Gongyan, representative of the Tianjin Shanghai Fellow Association Anti-Japanese Association, citizen representative Yang Ping, and representatives from the Chinese Literature and Art Society, Datong Bookstore striking workers, and two people from the Suisheng Match Company spoke one after another. The atmosphere at the meeting was very tense.

Public Security Bureau Car Patrol Team After the Disturbance (Captured by This Newspaper) 110

Key Resolutions After the report and speeches, the following resolutions were made on the spot: (1) Oppose accepting humiliating and power-losing conditions, oppose the Jinzhou neutral zone, oppose joint management of Tianjin, and oppose the neutral country investigation team; (2) Recover lost territory and let the people automatically arm themselves and declare war on Japan; (3) Deny the League of Nations plan, deny Shi as the representative of China, and deny Foreign Minister Gu; (4) Thoroughly sever economic ties, thoroughly boycott Japanese goods, organize people's inspection teams for Japanese goods, and auction off confiscated Japanese goods.

Large-Scale Riot At 3:30 pm, the meeting was adjourned. Various groups attending the meeting paraded and demonstrated. Rioters also infiltrated the parade, distributing reactionary leaflets, shouting reactionary slogans, and taking the opportunity to disrupt public order. The riot first started from the meeting place, heading east on Fang Xie Road, walking to the east side of the municipal party headquarters on Linyi Road. A French-owned tram number 3 of route 6 was parked in the middle of the road. The rioters immediately smashed the glass and car doors. Continuing west, past Ximen, they also destroyed Hua Shang tram numbers 38 of route 4, 34 of route 3, 40, 17, 14, 43, 26, route 2 public buses, municipal government notice numbers 4556, route 3 numbers 7406, 4284, car numbers 575, 831, and even a horse-drawn carriage with a bride sitting inside.

Police Chief Kidnapped Police Chief Liu of the second district and second precinct of the Municipal Public Security Bureau was standing at the Ximen intersection. When the parade passed, he was forcibly kidnapped by rioters, who forced him to participate in the riot. Police Chief Liu was unable to resist and was taken to Penglai Road. He was then rescued by the Municipal Public Security Bureau's police corps patrol team. Later, a sledgehammer, left behind by the rioters, was found in the round-trip trailer number 14 of Hua Shang tram route 3.

Prior Precautions The Municipal Public Security Bureau received a report in advance, saying that when the People's National Salvation Association held a citizen assembly, rioters would infiltrate it, intending to disrupt public order. The bureau immediately ordered the various districts, precincts, sub-precincts, police stations, and team leaders to take strict precautions. The authorities in the Public Concession and the French Concession also received the same report and also stepped up precautions yesterday.

Temporary Martial Law Because the Municipal Public Security Bureau had taken precautions in advance, when the parade and demonstration began, the police corps patrol team was already patrolling fully armed. They immediately went to suppress the riot and were able to disperse the rioters after reaching Penglai Road. The rioters took the opportunity to flee north without a trace. Temporary martial law was declared that evening.

The Xinming Ship Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Carrying Overseas Chinese Returning Home 111

A Total of One Thousand Two Hundred and Twenty-Five People

The Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau Arranged for Them to Reside in Various Guild Halls

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was ordered to send the Xinming Ship to Japan to carry overseas Chinese returning home. Yesterday morning, the ship arrived in Shanghai fully loaded with compatriots. The Social Affairs Bureau and various fellow associations went to take care of them and made arrangements for their accommodation. The details of each item are recorded as follows:

The Ship Arrived in Yokohama The Xinming Ship set sail on the 30th of last month to transport overseas Chinese to Japan. It arrived in Yokohama on the afternoon of the 5th. Chiang Tso-pin, the former Republic of China Minister to Japan, Ling Manshou, the Consul General in Yokohama, Zhou, the Consul General in Shincho, Bao Yingzhang, the Standing Committee Member of the Yokohama Branch directly under the Chinese Kuomintang, and Zhang Youfu, the representative of the Chinese Association, prepared various foods and welcomed the ship. On the evening of that day, they held a banquet at the Boyating Restaurant to welcome the ship's owner, Ma Jiajun, the first mate, Qian Yujia, and the acting business director, Wang Shanhai.

Overseas Chinese in Both Places At Yokohama, 693 male overseas Chinese, 77 female overseas Chinese, and 121 children were loaded onto the ship for their return home. At noon on the 7th, the ship left Yokohama for Kobe. It arrived in Kobe at 8 am on the 9th. Chinese groups were also very welcome. At that time, 188 male overseas Chinese, 59 female overseas Chinese, and 87 children were loaded onto the ship. A total of 1,225 people and more than 2,000 pieces of luggage were loaded from both places. The most were from Wenzhou and Taizhou in Zhejiang, followed by Ningbo, Fujian, Guangdong, and Jiangsu. At 4 pm on the 9th, the ship set sail from Kobe, traveled along the Inland Sea, passed through Moji, changed to the East China Sea, and returned home.

Encountered a Hurricane At around 10 pm on the 11th, the ship encountered a hurricane about 100 miles east of Hana Mountain. The Xinming Ship was quite dangerous in the wind and waves, and all the overseas Chinese were extremely panicked. The ship's owner, Ma Jiajun, tried to comfort the overseas Chinese. At the same time, in order to avoid danger, he drove slowly. All more than 100 staff members stayed up day and night. The ship was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at 12 pm on the 12th, but therefore arrived at Wusong at 1:30 am yesterday. It was late at night, so it anchored and stayed. It sailed into the Wusongkou at 6 am at dawn and arrived in Shanghai at 8:45 am, berthing at Pier No. 4 of Jinliyuan in the French Concession.

Arrangements Made The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau sent staff to the pier to take care of the returnees. The French Concession authorities sent detectives to maintain order. The Wenzhou, Taizhou, Ningbo, Guangdong, and Jiangsu Shanghai Fellow Associations, the Fujian Sanshan Guild Hall, and the Japanese Students' General Association sent staff to receive the returnees. The Social Affairs Bureau, together with various fellow associations, temporarily arranged for accommodation and issued food allowances in order to arrange for them to be sent back to their hometowns.

Situation in Japan A reporter from Xin Sheng She visited Wang Shanhai, the business director of the ship, yesterday. According to him, all procedures for this trip to Japan were completed by the commissioner Guo Waifeng, who telegraphed the consul in Japan. Therefore, when arriving in Yokohama, inspections such as quarantine were waived. The round trip took more than ten days and consumed more than 300 tons of coal and more than 50 piculs of rice. The Japanese were surprised to see that the Xinming Ship was managed entirely by Chinese people and showed their admiration. It is now scheduled to set sail as usual on the 15th to Weihai, Yantai, and Tianjin to load passengers. Commissioner Guo has already telegraphed the Ministry of Transportation and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to report the progress.

Eurasia Airplane's Northwest Test Flight Departed Northbound Yesterday Morning 112

With Dihua as the Endpoint, Over Four Thousand Li Long Li Jingcong, the operations group leader of Eurasia Airlines, departed from Hongqiao Airport on the Eurasia No. 3 aircraft at 11:30 am yesterday for a 4,200-li long northwest test flight. The Eurasia No. 3 aircraft paused briefly over Beijing, then flew directly to Beiping, where it transferred to the Eurasia No. 1 aircraft, passing through Bolin Temple, Ruoshui River, Hami, and then to Dihua. It is estimated that the voyage from Beiping to Dihua will take about four days, and it may return to Shanghai within the year.

Letter to the Nation from the University Students Anti-Japanese Joint Association 115

The Shanghai University Students Anti-Japanese National Salvation Joint Association's letter to the nation regarding the "January 29th Incident" reads:

Since the outbreak of Japanese aggression, the government has passively watched our great rivers and mountains shrink by a hundred miles each day, with countless compatriots being brutally massacred. Other than (calmness), there is nothing else to comfort the people of the nation. Students in Shanghai, unwilling to see the descendants of the Yellow Emperor perish in this way, acting on the principle of "Everyone is responsible for the fate of the nation," and standing on the position of the national revolutionary movement, organized the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Joint Association to awaken the people, rise together to seek survival, and train ourselves to prepare for national crisis. Furthermore, with diplomacy repeatedly failing and the situation becoming increasingly urgent, we twice went to Beijing to request that the government vigorously implement revolutionary diplomacy and resolutely send troops to resist the invaders. Our loyal and sincere heart and passionate spirit should be understood and appreciated by all compatriots. However, the Shanghai Special City Party Committee members, who have always regarded themselves as leaders of the people, at this critical moment of national crisis, should have恪遵 [respectfully followed] Sun Yat-sen's instructions to "not slacken day and night" and be the "vanguard for the people." Instead, they superficially guided and participated in the anti-Japanese national salvation movement of our association, but in reality, they interfered in every way possible, and their secret sabotage efforts were relentless. For example, during our association's second petition in Beijing, Education Director Zhang, representing Chairman Chiang, replied that he had not prevented students from coming to Beijing. However, the City Party Committee issued urgent instructions beforehand to strictly prevent and suppress. Unable to prevent it, they then made false accusations to the chief of the Executive Yuan, who openly affirmed that the petitioning group was deliberately causing trouble. Although they later declared it untrue, the students had no choice but to leave Beijing with tears in their eyes. As another example, when our association recently telegraphed Chairman Chiang, inquiring about the truth of the arrest of Peking University students and the humiliating diplomacy, the City Party Committee members instructed their lackeys to use economic blockade policies to delay the dispatch of the telegram for two days. These are the most obvious examples. However, our association believes that the urgent task at hand is to resist foreign aggression, and we have no time to question the motives of the City Party Committee's actions. We still endure humiliation and strive to do our best to understand. Unexpectedly, on the 9th of this month, when our association's 21st Delegates' Conference was held at the Youth Propaganda Corps, dozens of plainclothes detectives actually followed Committee Member Tao Baichuan of the City Party Committee into the venue. After the discussion of the third petition to Beijing was completed, Peking University representative Mr. Xu reported on the various oppressions suffered by Peking

Page 14

University students in Beijing and the news of their being tied up and escorted back to Peiping. When Central University representative Mr. Jiang reported the recent truth of the diplomatic situation, the plainclothes detectives shouted "Beat them!" Our association immediately implored Committee Member Tao to take responsibility for maintaining order, but Committee Member Tao ignored it. Our association, knowing that the environment was bad and that the members' freedom of speech was no longer safe, decided on the spot to "immediately change the venue," and the next day's delegates' conference was held at Jiaotong University. However, we still did not expect that the City Party Committee authorities, in broad daylight, would take extremely despicable and vicious measures to deal with the pure youths engaged in anti-Japanese national salvation. As soon as the meeting ended, Mr. Xu and Mr. Jiang stepped out, and the plainclothes detectives swarmed downstairs, colluding with the hooligans who had been lying in wait outside the door, kidnapped Mr. Xu, put him in a car, and sped away. Mr. Jiang was brutally beaten and covered in wounds. Thanks to the rescue of all the representatives of our association, he was spared. At the time, there were many assailants, and they were armed. Our association was unable to arrest all of them, but only captured Wang Fusheng and handed him over to the police station for custody. After the incident, the entire association was extremely indignant and immediately went to the Public Security Bureau to question why they had not provided protection beforehand and why they had not helped to arrest the perpetrators afterward. At that time, Director Chen Xizeng replied, "The City Party Committee notified the Student Federation to send police for protection at each meeting in the past. This time, we did not receive a notification, so it was not convenient to send police. If the Public Security Bureau personnel were negligent afterward, they will be punished according to the law," etc. Our association pondered this repeatedly and firmly believed that the instigator of this unfortunate incident must be the Shanghai Special City Party Committee. The various reasons are listed as follows: (1) The City Party Committee must notify the police to protect the meeting in the past. Why was this time an exception? (2) Committee Member Tao Baichuan of the City Party Committee must wait for the meeting to end before leaving in the past. Why did he leave beforehand this time? (3) When plainclothes detectives disrupted the meeting, our association asked Committee Member Tao to stop them. Why did he ignore it? (4) Why did Committee Member Tao publicly slander the second petition at our association's meeting? (5) Our association has repeatedly decided that non-school representatives may not attend, but Committee Member Tao deliberately disrupted this proposal first, causing our association to be unable to implement this resolution and drive the plainclothes detectives out of the venue (although the venue of the Youth Propaganda Corps is for everyone to speak, since a group has borrowed it, it should be able to prevent bystanders from listening). (6) There are several Party Committee cadres among the perpetrators. (7) The perpetrators rested in the Public Security Bureau. (8) Why did City Party Committee officials pose as student representatives to participate in the disruption? Based on the above reasons, the responsibility for the incident is known to everyone. Our association deeply grieves the trampling of the young students and the escalating sabotage of the patriotic movement. Therefore, that night, we sent 5,000 students to inquire about the reasons from the City Party Committee, but to no avail. We also asked the Municipal Government for the following four conditions: (1) Do not suppress the anti-Japanese movement. (2) Release the arrested students. (3) Punish the Director of the Public Security Bureau. (4) Punish the City Party Committee personnel. Mayor Zhang then ordered the suspension of Public Security Bureau Director Chen Xizeng for investigation and ordered the arrest of Tao Baichuan for trial. All the students then straightened their ranks and stood all night in the Municipal Government Square, waiting for the release of the arrested students. On the morning of the 10th, upon Mayor Zhang's instruction, our association sent five representatives, together with Municipal Government representatives Sun Baorong and Guo Rui, to organize a temporary court and extract the perpetrator Wang Fusheng from the court for interrogation. Knowing that the evidence was conclusive and undeniable, the perpetrator voluntarily confessed the truth, saying, "I am a party member and was ordered by Xie, Gu, and other party members to suppress the patriotic movement." At 10:00 a.m., Peking University arrested student Mr. Xu was found by Secretary-General Yu and brought to the Municipal Government, where he immediately reported the process of his arrest to the public, saying, "The Public Security Bureau, on the order of the City Party Committee, kidnapped me and escorted me to Pudong and Dongjiadu Wharf, etc., Jiangxin." Then Mayor Zhang came out and addressed the entire association, saying, "I myself have never suppressed the patriotic movement. This incident was entirely caused by Public Security Bureau Director Chen Xizeng deliberately deceiving and being exploited by others. It is truly heartbreaking." His attitude was extremely sincere at the time, and the students were very moved. They then immediately asked the mayor to set a deadline for arresting Chen and Tao. The mayor replied, "I am responsible for arresting Chen and Tao within three days and handing them over to the temporary court for interrogation." All the students believed that the reply was satisfactory, shouted slogans, and returned to school in formation. This is the general situation of the "January 29th Incident." After this, our association believed even more that the Shanghai City Party Committee and the Public Security Bureau should bear full responsibility for this unfortunate incident. The reasons are further stated on the left: (1) When some students petitioned the City Party Committee, why did Committee Member Tao Baichuan refuse to meet and escape through the back door? If he was not afraid of guilt and vanity, how could he do this? (2) "Party members have no personal freedom." The perpetrator Wang Fusheng confessed that he and other accomplices were all party members. It is clear that they were instructed by the Party Committee. If the Party Committee believes that Wang's and others' acts of violence were individual actions, why has it not enforced strict party discipline and severely punished them since the incident? (3) According to the report of Peking University representative Mr. Xu and the speech of Mayor Zhang, there is no doubt that the City Party Committee instructed the Public Security Bureau to commit the crime. Alas, the facts are now as clear as fire. If the Kuomintang still has party discipline and the National Government still has laws, it will arrest and interrogate Chen, Tao, and other moths who sabotage the national salvation movement in the shortest possible time and execute them according to the law. Our association takes anti-Japanese national salvation as its banner. If the running dogs of the Japanese invaders are not eliminated for a day, our association's responsibility will not be fulfilled for a day. In the future, no matter how Tao, Chen, etc., spread rumors and slander, and retaliate to their heart's content, our association will lead all Shanghai students to fight them to the death and will never evade. Tao, Chen, etc., are corrupt and incompetent and have been doing evil for many years. Their tricks are only up to this point. We hope that all compatriots will see through their treachery, rise up together to denounce them, pacify the interior and resist the foreigners, and carry out both in parallel. The future of the nation and its substantial benefits depend on this. This is our declaration.

Justice was not served, and people were panicking. Defending the soil and guarding the homeland is a win-win situation. It can also encourage the people's morale. The mournful horn of the warhorse is enough to await the urgent order. In the autumn of the country's survival, although the association's power is weak, it will do its best to promote saving the country from danger to the people and is not without small help. I respectfully offer this declaration.

County Government Urgently Collecting Arrears of Grain Tax 123

The Shanghai County winter grain tax collection office opened on the 5th of this month. Subsequently, the bureau found that the amount of busy silver in the 20th year and the old arrears of last year's busy grain tax were still huge. Now, it has received a telegram from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance stating that the provincial treasury is empty, and the administrative expenses of various agencies are without funds. In addition to borrowing winter grain tax from Wuxi and other counties, all provincial tax arrears in the county must be strictly urged to be paid to the treasury by the deadline. Therefore, Director Wang of the bureau yesterday specifically ordered the urging officials to inform the township chiefs to urge and collect all old arrears from the busy grain tax collection period as soon as possible and pay them in full. If there are stubborn households who deliberately delay payment, they will be reported and prosecuted to emphasize the national tax.

Scholarship Association Announces Essay Contest 126

Each Prize: Two Hundred Yuan

First Set of Three Economics Questions

Yu Huancheng, Zhang Sumin, Jin Jingyang, Zhu Qinglai, Zhang Gangbo, Liu Hongsheng, Qin Tongli, Li Zuyu, Zhang Oufang, Guo Yushang, Xue Xuejin, and others, recognizing the difficulty faced by impoverished students in pursuing advanced learning, have initiated a Scholarship Association. It will be divided into social science, natural science, and literature categories, with essay contests held monthly. The selection of topics and grading of papers will be handled by experts. Each essay contest will offer a prize of two hundred yuan, with approximately one hundred yuan awarded to the first-place winner. The remaining amount will be determined based on the number of outstanding entries. The association has already secured sufficient funds for a year's worth of prizes. The first essay contest topics, related to economics, have been drafted by Dr. Zhang Sumin and others. They are listed below:

(First Question) Modern, commonly accepted economics is mostly based on the theories of the neoclassical school, with slight modifications. However, there has been considerable criticism in recent times, with some even creating a new institutionalist school. What are the origins of this so-called commonly accepted economics? What is its theoretical system? What are its research methods and objects of study? What are the points of attack made by critics? What is the basis of their arguments? What does the institutionalist school emphasize? What methods do they employ? To what extent has it developed today? Please elaborate on this.

(Second Question) The rickshaw puller is a difficult problem in our country's labor issues. Conduct personal interviews with fifty to one hundred rickshaw pullers or their family members in your city. Accurately investigate the following items, as well as any other items you deem necessary, and list them in a table for detailed discussion. Present the crux of the rickshaw puller problem and methods for its resolution. (1) The occupation of the rickshaw puller's father; (2) The rickshaw puller's age; (3) The rickshaw puller's education; (4) The rickshaw puller's experience; (5) The rickshaw puller's family size; (6) The rickshaw puller's income; (7) The rickshaw puller's expenses; (8) The rickshaw puller's working hours; (9) The period during which the rickshaw puller pulls the rickshaw; (10) The rickshaw puller's illnesses; (11) The rickshaw puller's other skills; (12) The rickshaw puller's organization.

(Third Question) An economic severance with Japan is widely considered an essential measure for national salvation. Within this economic severance, boycotting Japanese goods is of utmost importance. Which Japanese goods can be replaced with domestic products? Which can only be temporarily replaced with goods from other countries? How do their uses and prices compare to Japanese goods? How can consumers be protected from losses and permanently maintain the boycott? Furthermore, for imitation foreign goods that use Japanese raw materials, what alternative sources of raw materials can be used? How do their uses and prices compare to Japanese goods? Can they be self-sufficient and self-manufactured? What are the costs of self-manufacture? Please conduct a detailed investigation of the categories, sales volume, value, function, and comparison with substitutes, as well as the costs of self-manufacture, and present them in two separate tables: A, Commodities; B, Raw materials for imitation foreign goods. Each table should list ten kinds of Japanese goods as a passing grade. The tables should include the following items: (1) Name of the Japanese good; (2) Sales volume; (3) Price (indicate the unit); (4) Function; (5) What substitute can be used; (6) How the function of the substitute compares to the Japanese good; (7) How the price of the substitute compares to the Japanese good; (8) Difficulty of self-manufacture; (9) Estimated cost of self-manufacture; (10) Projected price of self-manufactured product (indicate the unit). Add explanations after each table.

It is reported that the first question includes a bibliography, and the second question includes explanatory notes, as well as essay contest regulations and award methods. All information is published in the New Society Bi-Monthly, Issue 12, published on the 16th of this month. Those wishing to participate in the essay contest should refer to the New Society, Issue 12, published at 142 Weihaiwei Road, Shanghai.
